  <span id="freeText12498544824499170620" style="display:none"><br />My review can also be found on my blog <a href="http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2013/02/reviews-something-like-normal-by-trish.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Collections</a>.<br /><br />I love Thomas. Out of all the boys in <i>Saving Francesca</i>, it was definitely Thomas who stood out to me. Really happy to know more about him and his situation, including the rest of his family's. Melina Marchetta is always so great with family and friend relationships.<br /><br />I also loved the parts with Thomas and the other characters from <i>Saving Francesca</i>, especially Tara, the girls, and Will Trombal. But I love that there's always hope in the end and that you just know it will all eventually work out for the characters. Seriously can't wait to read Marchetta's next book. Love them all!<br /><br />(And I'm with everyone who says that we need Jimmy's story! PLEASE!!)</span>

<div id="review_209428650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209428650" />
    <a title="Carla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2352516-carla"><img alt="Carla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601068789p2/2352516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209428650?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carla" href="/user/show/2352516-carla">Carla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2352516-carla?shelf=aussie-ya">aussie-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2352516-carla?shelf=forever-love">forever-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2352516-carla?shelf=queen-of-ya">queen-of-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209428650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17146710170983756693">Confession – writing this was terrifying. I love this book in an intense unexplainable way that makes me nervous. It makes me selfish, clutching my thoughts to my chest, unwilling to share them because they are mine and you can’t have them. This book is my secret and it’s time I came clean.<br/><br/>There is a reason why Marchetta is my favourite author and it extends beyond her skills as a writer. It is her ability to read people; to strip back the layers and lay them bare. She doesn’t box them into trop</span>
  <span id="freeText17146710170983756693" style="display:none">Confession – writing this was terrifying. I love this book in an intense unexplainable way that makes me nervous. It makes me selfish, clutching my thoughts to my chest, unwilling to share them because they are mine and you can’t have them. This book is my secret and it’s time I came clean.<br /><br />There is a reason why Marchetta is my favourite author and it extends beyond her skills as a writer. It is her ability to read people; to strip back the layers and lay them bare. She doesn’t box them into tropes or smother them in stereotypes, she writes people as they are; real. So that is what they become. Her ability to write every facet of the human condition breathes so much life into her characters that they cease to be words on a page. Nothing is idealised, every emotion is raw and unflinchingly real.<br /><br />Tom’s relationship with his father was this all-encompassing thing that transcended beyond the words on the page. That confusing heart breaking realisation that this person you admire is just that; a person. They will hurt you in ways you never thought possible and it will cut deep, until the you recognise that even the adults amongst us make mistakes. Their relationship is painful and beautiful all at once, because it’s gone from being this wonderful thing full of trust and communication to complete silence. And it’s the breakdown of their relationship, how it hit rock bottom then carried on going for good measure that permeates Tom in ways he doesn't really understand. Those Finch-Mackees will get you good.<br /><br />And not forgetting his life outside of his family, which is as much of an emotional driving force for the story as the inner workings of the Finch-Mackee clan. And that comes in the form of his relationship with his school friends aka the four horsewomen, Francesca, Justine, Siobhan and Tara, and not forgetting one Will Trombal. (IT IS GOOD TO BE BACK GUYS, OH HOW I HAVE MISSED YOU). He needs them to talk him down and welcome him back into the fold, because these are not fleeting friendships, these are friendships built on solid foundations that won’t ever fail. They are nuanced and vivid and it’s like stumbling across a secret that you knew but forgot. Their interactions are alive and will slay you with their humor. They are in a word, mesmorising. I could quite happily sit in the corner of the Union and just watch them and never get bored.<br /><br />Georgie, she snuck up on me and held fast and tight. Her character was woven through with grief and guilt so cloying that it sometimes hurt my heart to read. She’s the lighthouse in the storm guiding you home but she too is broken and unwilling to forgive, even if forgiving means finding the way back to her. She overwhelmed me this woman, because she shows that even adults sometimes don’t get it right and sometimes all you can do is try to hold things together the best that you can.<br /><br />The essence of this story is love – the love between family that more often than not gets taken for granted. The love between friends that stays strong regardless of the passing of time or distance. And it’s about the pain that love can inflict upon a person; grief, disappointment, misunderstandings. All the different ways you can inadvertently hurt those who mean the most. There is nothing harder than watching grief tear a family to shreds and having to look at the mess that was once something amazing. And Marchetta gets that and she doesn’t try to romanticise the spite and the hate that comes with loss, she never ones tries to make it anything less than what it is; it’s ugly and brutal and it can diminish a person.<br /><br />There are some moments in life that make you stop and marvel – they’re few and far between and if you’re not paying enough attention, they might just pass you by. This book is a marvel and even if I could recite it off by heart, I would never, not ever, be able to do this book justice. This is my secret. And now it is yours. <br /><br />(p.s Jimmy, I love you. Let's have tea and talk fantasy fiction. I know you're not a pothead.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17146710170983756693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127277152" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127277152" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127277152?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Street Corner Bookers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arlene by: </span>
      Albie Thank you!!!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127277152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15182573615333365689"><i>Maybe she’d always been there. Maybe strangers enter your heart first and then you spend the rest of your life searching for them. - TM</i><br/><br/>I don’t know how she does it, but Marchetta delivers it every time - a fictional story that seems so real, a cast of characters you’re not ready to let go of, and a powerful dialog that reaches into your heart and soul and reveals lessons and observations that have you contemplating love, life, loss and redemption. Absolute and shear perfection that I will never </span>
  <span id="freeText15182573615333365689" style="display:none"><i>Maybe she’d always been there. Maybe strangers enter your heart first and then you spend the rest of your life searching for them. - TM</i><br /><br />I don’t know how she does it, but Marchetta delivers it every time - a fictional story that seems so real, a cast of characters you’re not ready to let go of, and a powerful dialog that reaches into your heart and soul and reveals lessons and observations that have you contemplating love, life, loss and redemption. Absolute and shear perfection that I will never get enough of.<br /><br /><b>The Piper’s Son</b> is a heart-wrenching story told in alternating POVs of both Thomas Mackee and Georgie Finch. It takes place two years after the death of Thomas’ Uncle Joe and the day he walked away from his friends from St. Sebastians and his family that was on the verge of imploding. Georgie has a set of issues of her own as her pregnancy progresses and she struggles to make sense of her life and the man that cheated on her seven years prior. This story takes you on their journey, one of healing, forgiveness and finding one’s way home again. <br /><br />As with Marchetta’s other books, I love the cast of characters she creates and every single one is a gem in their own right. They are full of surprises and ready to take you on their exploration of life. I loved the twist with Mohsin the Ignorer. It made me realize that the worst thing you can do is not give someone a chance or simply the benefit of the doubt. Wow, when his bit was revealed, I was this close *gestures thumb and index finger one inch apart* to starting the story from the beginning to get a different perspective. <br /><br />Frankie, Tara, Justine and Will were fun to revisit, but I wish.wish.wish Jimmy would have made an appearance. But no worries, this book delivered a healthy dose of surprises, sigh-worthy moments, and misty eyes that I hope others will enjoy as much as I did.<br /><br />Melina Marchetta, the words you to commit to page are magical and the journeys you deliver are heart rending. You are a literary genius!!<br /><br /><b>Final note:</b> A big HUG and thank you my kiwi friend Albie for sending me this beauteous book all the way from New Zealand. You are the bestest and I ♥ you for sharing this wonderful book with me!! It is South Carolina bound to the next SC Booker because it deserves to be shared and cherished. Alexa, you're up! :)<br /><br /><b>Favorite quotes</b><br /><i>Don’t let anyone take care of you. Can you maybe leave that for me to do? I mean, take care of you? Feel free to take care of me in return… because I think I’ll need you to do that.- TM<br /><br />Death by humiliation... - TM</i><br /><br /><i>Play me something that makes me feel,<br />This soul inside is made of steel.<br />Brain is breathing, but heart’s not beating,<br />And babe I need you to make things real.<br /><br />Walk inside me without silence,<br />Kill the past and change the tense.<br />Empty gnawing and the ache is soaring,<br />Take me places that make more sense.<br />-Thomas Mackee</i></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_169145755" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169145755" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169145755?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780763647582" href="/book/show/9302583-the-piper-s-son">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169145755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2166292769825281902"><i>"But this beat is fast and even though his joints are aching, his arm's out of control like it has a mind of its own and the sweat that drenches his hair and face seem to smother him, but nothing's going to stop Tom. He's aiming for oblivion.”</i><br/><br/><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>I feel so very stricken. How does MM do these things to my soul? <br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>Thomas Finch Mackee. Family. History. Honesty. Grief. Reality. Late night phone calls. Sydney International Airport. Attics. E-Mails. Impossible questio</span>
  <span id="freeText2166292769825281902" style="display:none"><i>"But this beat is fast and even though his joints are aching, his arm's out of control like it has a mind of its own and the sweat that drenches his hair and face seem to smother him, but nothing's going to stop Tom. He's aiming for oblivion.”</i><br /><br /><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />I feel so very stricken. How does MM do these things to my soul? <br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />Thomas Finch Mackee. Family. History. Honesty. Grief. Reality. Late night phone calls. Sydney International Airport. Attics. E-Mails. Impossible questions. Getting the right chord. <br /><br /><b>Low Point.</b><br />Two thoughts: <br />Ugh, yeah, I really don’t like Will.<br />and<br />WHERE WAS JIMMY?!<br /><br /><b>Hero.</b><br />I feel like I need to quote Tara Finke here before I start what will be known as the ‘Torrent of Love for Tom F. Mackee’. <br /><blockquote>“Thomas Mackee is the last bastion of arrested development and hormonal retardation.” (SF)</blockquote><br />Thomas Finch Mackee is not a likeable character. If you met him in the street, you’d probably want to punch him or shake him or slap him or just yell at him until your lungs are raw because he is so infuriating. He makes terrible decisions, he has no definite goals, he’s callous and he’s an awful, awful, awful friend/son/nephew/boyfriend (nearly wrote ‘lover’ then, but you <i>know</i> that would have been a lie ;-) )<br />But from page one of this book (I’m ignoring Saving Francesca here because I think I made my love for him clear in <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com/2011/07/saving-francesca-melina-marchetta.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> ), I fell in love with him all over again, in spite of all his flaws. Maybe even <i>because</i> of his flaws. <br />He’s confused, he’s angry, he’s sad and he’s desperate and if this was any other book or any other writer I would’ve been like “Urgh, just sort your life out preferably somewhere where I’m not” but every time Tom was hurting, my heart completely broke and my gut wrenched and all of those t’other metaphors. <br />Thus is the power of Ms Marchetta. <i>Witchcraft, I say. </i><br />I think it would be easy for people to not like Tom, and even though <s>I’d think you were completely loopy</s> I would understand, it’s important to remember that this book finds Tom at rock bottom and it is his journey through his grief and learning to forgive and love that makes Tom, and this book, so perfect in my eyes.<br /><br /><b>Georgie. </b><br />Ohh, Georgie. I loved how she was just as flawed as the rest of them and made no apologies. Her entire world is falling apart around her and she’s a mess, but she still gets there in the end. I love how the relationship between the past, the present and the future of her family were depicted through Georgie. <br />And those e-mails?<br />Sob.<br />Also, some of the exchanges between Georgie and Tom were absolutely hilarious. Their dynamic was really excellent. <br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />Tara Finke. The girl who <i>“makes his heart beat fast”</i>. It’s difficult to talk about Finke because, bar a few pages, she isn’t actually in this book as a real person but more of a memory and a blatant reminder to Tom at how far he had fallen and screwed up everything that was important to him. <br />But the rambling e-mails and late-night phone calls were highly entertaining and extremely sweet.<br /><br /><b>Jimmy.</b><br />Yes, he gets his own heading because there was a blatant Jimmy-shaped hole missing in this book. Although… I <i>did</i> notice on page 127 that Francesca says “Jim doesn’t want to be found just yet.”<br />Hm. Just yet, eh? <br />I’m going to hold out for a book purely about Thomas Mackee and Jimmy Hailler <s>and Jonah Griggs</s> and the road trip they go on to reconnect and bond. Also on this road trip they would inexplicably find themselves in Manchester. *shifty look*<br /><br /><b>Theme Tune.</b><br />OK, I think I need to create a Thomas Finch Mackee playlist because I have approximately a million songs I want to <s>listen to with him while we’re sat in Georgie’s attic surrounded by all his crap</s> link with him.<br />But I’ve narrowed it down to two.<br />Well… technically fourteen.<br />My theme <i>album</i> for him would be <u>Urban Hymns</u> by The Verve. Every song on this album is beautiful and raw and passionate and brutal and poetic and I like to think that Tom would appreciate the ridiculously amazing musical composition that goes into every single one of their songs. And also, I think the conflicts that were rife in between the band members have a certain kind of resonance with Tom’s character and his own destructive relationships. <br />If I had to pick <i>one</i> song from the album it would be this one.<br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MH6TJU0qWoY&amp;ob=av2e" rel="nofollow noopener">Lucky Man- The Verve.</a><br /><br />And, um… <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1lyu1KKwC74" rel="nofollow noopener">this one.</a><br /><br />And the other song choice stems from my thoughts about Tom’s relationship with his dad which stood out to me as the one that was most the poignant.<br />Marchetta’s portrayal of the breakdown of Tom’s relationship with his dad, who had been placed on such a high pedestal, was so perfectly executed that every scene the two of them were in together made me <s>sob like a girl</s> feel very sad. There was such a bitter-sweet tinge to every conversation and every look and every memory they had together. <br />So this song is dedicated to Tom and the piper and I hope that one day they will return to how they used to and Tom will want to follow his hero once more. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=k3WhQB7Hq0Q" rel="nofollow noopener">JCB Song- Nizlopi.</a><br /><br /><b>Angst Level.</b><br />10/10. There isn’t much I can say about this that I haven’t already mentioned or that I don’t want to spoil. This book doesn’t hold any prisoners and it doesn’t offer any easy quick-fix answers or solutions to the issues that are brought up. <br />This book is a refreshing change from the typical YA book, especially because not only is Tom older than the usual YA hero (he’s twenty one) but we also have the perspective of Georgie, who is in her early forties. <br /><br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />Everyone. People who haven’t read Saving Francesca (or, people who <i>have</i> read SF, I just mean you don’t need to have read it because even though there are overlaps… this is Tom’s book). People who have a thing for bad boys. People who think it’s a crime to rhyme. People who come and go and talk of Michaelangelo. People who can read about Norton Anthologies without having heart palpitations (the horror… the horroooor). People who wish that there was a key on your computer to stop an e-mail being sent once you pressed ‘Send’. People who instantly think of watching Neighbours when they’re supposed to be writing essays when they read the word ‘pash’. People who wish more people would read this book so they didn’t think they were a mental when they announce that “It’s time to STD’. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2166292769825281902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_538539534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538539534" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538539534?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">New Adult fans who want to see realistic fiction done right</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=goddamn-onions">goddamn-onions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=foreign-setting">foreign-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538539534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4637209321891005771"><b>
  <i>4.5 STARS</i>
</b><br/><br/>I came in this book, expecting a guffaws-a-minute marathon with Thomas Mackee, the "last bastion of patriarchal poor taste, arrested development and mental retardation". So it took me a couple of chapters to get into the groove of things seeing as this is actually a story about Tom AND his aunt Georgie, 5 years after <i>Saving Francesca</i>, living in the years after the death of a beloved family member. That and every possible issue you can cram in a New Adult-Adult book: family, friendsh</span>
  <span id="freeText4637209321891005771" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>4.5 STARS</i>
</b><br><br>I came in this book, expecting a guffaws-a-minute marathon with Thomas Mackee, the "last bastion of patriarchal poor taste, arrested development and mental retardation". So it took me a couple of chapters to get into the groove of things seeing as this is actually a story about Tom AND his aunt Georgie, 5 years after <i>Saving Francesca</i>, living in the years after the death of a beloved family member. That and every possible issue you can cram in a New Adult-Adult book: family, friendship, love, honor, sex, religion, loss, grief, betrayal, forgiveness… racial stereotypes? I'm thinking back on that scene where Tom finally confronts Mohsin and I'll also have to put a check on that one. <br><br>Having read a fair amount of the New Adult books out there that claims to be realistic has somewhat skewed my expectations on what realistic is. The first half of this book, I couldn't understand the ripples created by the death of Joe, Tom's uncle, and the recovery of the body of one Tom Finch, Tom's biological grandfather. From Vietnam. I couldn't relate to the bonds these 2 characters have forged to the players in this story.<br><br>Because standard "realistic" New Adult fare means it's the mom or the dad and a car crash or cancer or infidelity or alcohol or abuse… and hey, sometimes, when you're really lucky, all of the above, that fuels the drama in the story. Then the a**hole hero falls for his best friend, no the other bestfriend who has a boyfriend overseas. And who cares about the other adults in the family? They're old, they have nothing interesting to offer the story. Then tension, tension, sex… then cliffhanger.<br><br>Get ready to be reprogrammed.<br><br>Because these two seemingly unrelated events are like separate storms, and you're standing there with Tom and Georgie, weathering through their effects on mothers, fathers, cheating boyfriends, almost girlfriends and the people they survive the day to day with in the aftermath of regrets, foraging through the pain of loss and embracing the unassuming comfort offered by the unlikeliest of friends.<br><br>It sounds heavy, I know and it is. Marchetta does what she does best: telling you a heartbreaking story,make you comfortable with amusing banter, then kick your heart broken to pieces again so she can patch them up good to break. Again. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>And then she's crying. Just crying and crying like everyone in his life does these days. He walks around her desk and hugs her. Vows there'll never be a reason for him to treat her the way he has. Because he doesn't want her crying like this ever again.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>And again. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Am I worth the hard w--?"<br>"Yes," he says before she finishes. "Yes."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>But there's an art to how Marchetta delivers those gutting moments. The gentlest comforting laughter and humor so that when she's starting that littlest pinch in your heart, you don't notice until you're already bleeding some.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Frankie will choose the two shittiest songs each time, just to piss us off," Tom mutters.<br>There's a sound of disgust from the front seat. "What a thing to say, Tom. Since when have I been that petty, huh?" She turns to Justine. "Can you believe he said that? Can you?<br>"Say you're sorry, Tom," Justine says.<br>He says he's sorry and Francesca plays Avril Lavigne's "Sk8r Boi".</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I cannot, in good conscience, recommend this to everyone. I have a bit of a pause weighing if this should be a 4 or a 5, but decisive enough to shelve it a favorite. But I have a feeling opinion will be divided on this one among my friends. The story is told in a non-linear fashion, lots of flashbacks that feels disjointed. One could even fashion a game out of it where you could cut up the flashbacks and arrange them in proper, linear chronology. It's not an easy read where you can't predict anything. Georgie is a 42-year old woman who got knocked up for the first time. Tom is a uni dropout, working as a dishwasher while his family's in tatters and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tara Finke is in East Timor with a Brazilian boyfriend <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I don't know anyone in real life in these predicaments but the small effort to understand their stories makes me feel like I already do.<br><br>Is it worth it then? The confusion at length? The gutting moments? The characters you can't seem to understand or care for at first? If only to read someone like Tom Mackee say this to someone like<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tara Finke? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Don't let anyone take care of you. Can you maybe leave that for me to do? I mean. take care of you? Feel free to take care of me in return… because I think I'll need you to do that."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Then yes. A thousand times, yes.<br><br>This one's for you, Tom.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410033ra/803429.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4637209321891005771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205160016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205160016" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205160016?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205160016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10356010436936961152"><br/>My love affair with Melina Marchetta continues! :D<br/><br/>Her words, style, and voices make my heart beat faster, stomach drop and twist, and head whirl with thoughts and memories. The tone and feel of her words just fit right in my heart. Her stories seem to pulse with this coiled intensity—a gritty beat that creeps up on me, sticks in my gut, and makes me smile, laugh or cry. Just when I think the sadness is going to overcome me, she throws in a jab of sly humor that makes me laugh out loud. I just lo</span>
  <span id="freeText10356010436936961152" style="display:none"><br />My love affair with Melina Marchetta continues! :D<br /><br />Her words, style, and voices make my heart beat faster, stomach drop and twist, and head whirl with thoughts and memories. The tone and feel of her words just fit right in my heart. Her stories seem to pulse with this coiled intensity—a gritty beat that creeps up on me, sticks in my gut, and makes me smile, laugh or cry. Just when I think the sadness is going to overcome me, she throws in a jab of sly humor that makes me laugh out loud. I just love how she talks to us. <br /><br />Sometimes it takes a bit for me to warm up and trust someone, but once you are in my heart you stay there—that is true in life and my fiction. It took me awhile to warm up to Georgie’s voice, but believe me—once I did, she slid right in, snuggled up to my heart and squeezed the hell out of it! Georgie’s story will forever have a place in my heart. The Mackee family is a lot to handle, but once they capture your heart—they are in there! <br /><br />Tom, on the other hand, had me at his first scene in Saving Francesca. He makes me smile just saying his name. I love how we get to know Tom through his relationships with his family, friends, music, and memories. Marchetta paints a sad, broken picture of a young man lost in grief, but starting to reach out. How Tom feels about the women in his life will make you swoon and “awww”. The boy could be the sweetest thing I have come across in young adult literature! I LOVE Thomas Mackee! :)<br /><br />Truth be told though, this book had my heart with two lines.<br /><br />“Sisters and daughters come second in this family, Tom. They always have.” <br /><br />“Wives can replace their husbands, Georgie, her aunt once told her. But sisters can’t replace their brothers.”<br /><br />All my time reading in this world, I have never come across these themes in print. Never said so loud and clear. Melina Marchetta just made me a fan for life. :)<br /><br />Please pick up Piper’s Son and see what she pokes, rattles, and shakes free from your soul.<br /><br />See what she does to your heart.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10356010436936961152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FwaLAAQh6KCPuNte9DMkPymkqgYFx0Xi9lo3f9TObMJnFTkz0DQ24ARfy7XY3UM3Dqy9wUtThOtZMDMpc0c//g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KKedXxNmiH2N1rErwZcOOPa92Kq/oaXGxuBci9ksBOhYtC9sx3NWPQYxocDteWkw0bXPbfE1ZM9piljdfqVX1A==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta">About Melina Marchetta</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1277655889p3/47104.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13097256899579486952">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the </span>
  <span id="freeText13097256899579486952" style="display:none">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the Jellicoe Road was released in 2006 and won the US Printz Medal in 2009 for excellence in YA literature. This was followed up by Finnikin of the Rock in 2008 which won the Aurealis Award for YA fantasy, The Piper's Son in 2010 which was shortlisted for the Qld Premier's Lit Award, NSW Premier's Lit Award, Prime Minister's Literary Awards, CBC awards and longlisted for the Miles Franklin Award. Her follow up to Finnikin, Froi of the Exiles and Quintana of Charyn were released in 2012 and 2013. Her latest novel Tell the Truth, Shame the Devil is an adult crime novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13097256899579486952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
